### Candidate 1: P*c0*exp(c1*t) + P*c2 + c3*t/(c4+t) + c5/(c4+t) + c6*t/(c4+t)

Simplify: P*c0*exp(c1*t) + P*c2 + (c3+c6)*t/(c4+t) + c5/(c4+t)

The rational-in-P term P²/(aP+1) requires P-dependent rational structure. This candidate has no P-dependent rational terms — only P*exp, P*linear, and t-dependent rational terms. The GT's second term depends on P in a nonlinear way (P²/(aP+1)), which cannot be represented by P*c2 + functions_of_t_only.

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 2: Similar to Candidate 1 with extra t*exp(c8*t) term. Same issue — no nonlinear P dependence.

Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 3: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*exp(c4/(c5+t))

Has P*exp(c2*t) ✓, P*c0 ✓, but c3*exp(c4/(c5+t)) is a function of t only. The GT needs a P²/(aP+1) term which is a nonlinear function of P. This can't match.

Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 4: P*c0*exp(c1*t) + P*c2 + c3*exp(P*c4 + c5*t)

The term c3*exp(P*c4 + c5*t) = c3*exp(c5*t)*exp(c4*P). If c4=0, this becomes c3*exp(c5*t), losing P dependence. The GT needs P²/(aP+1) which is rational in P, not exponential. exp(c4*P) ≠ rational function of P.

Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 5: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t)

Only two terms, both linear in P. Missing the P²/(aP+1) nonlinear term.

Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 6: P*c0*exp(c1*t) + P*c2 + P*c3*exp(P*c4) + c5*t/(c6+t) + c7/(c6+t) + c8*t/(c6+t)

Has P*c3*exp(P*c4). If c4=0, this becomes P*c3, just adding to P*c2. Can't produce P²/(aP+1). exp(P*c4) is not rational in P.

Candidate 6 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 7: P²*c0*t^c1 + P*c2*exp(c3*t) + P*c4*t^c5 + P*c6*t^c1 + c7*t

Has P*exp(c3*t) ✓. For the P²/(aP+1) term: we need it to be independent of t. P²*c0*t^c1 depends on t unless c1=0, giving P²*c0. But P² ≠ P²/(aP+1). The remaining terms P*c4*t^c5 + P*c6*t^c1 + c7*t can't create the 1/(aP+1) denominator.

Candidate 7 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 8: P*c0*exp(c1*t) + P*c2*t^c3 + c4*t + c5/(c6+t)

No nonlinear P dependence for the rational term.

Candidate 8 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 9: P^c0*c1 + P^c2*c3*sin(c4*t+c5) + c6*t² + c7*t + c8

Has sin(c4*t+c5) — GT has exp(-c1*t). These are different basis functions. sin can't match exp for all t. Even if c4=0, sin(c5) is constant, and P^c0*c1 + constant*P^c2 can't match P*exp(-ct) + P²/(aP+1).

Candidate 9 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 10: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*exp(c4/(c5+t)) + c6*exp(c7/P^(1/5))

Has P*exp(c2*t) ✓, P*c0 ✓. The term c6*exp(c7/P^(1/5)) is a function of P only. Can exp(c7/P^(1/5)) match P²/(aP+1) - (linear in P terms)? No — exp(c7/P^(1/5)) is transcendental in P while P²/(aP+1) is rational. And c3*exp(c4/(c5+t)) is t-only, adding unwanted t-dependence unless c3=0. If c3=0, we have P*(c0) + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c6*exp(c7/P^(1/5)). The exp function can't equal a rational function of P.

Candidate 10 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 11: P*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*exp(c3*t)*log(P*c4+1) + c5*exp(c6/(c7+t)) + c8*exp(c9/P^(1/5))

The term P*c2*exp(c3*t)*log(P*c4+1) mixes t and P in a way GT doesn't (GT's exp term is P*exp, not P*exp*log(P)). Setting c4=0 makes log(1)=0, killing the term. Then we'd need the exp(c9/P^(1/5)) to handle the P² rational term — can't work.

### Candidate 17: P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + c3 + c4*t + c5*log(P*c6+1) + c7/P

Let me check this carefully. P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) gives us rational P dependence. 

P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) = [c0*P*(P+c2) + c1*P]/(P+c2) = [c0*P² + (c0*c2+c1)*P]/(P+c2)

GT's P-dependent part (at t→∞ where exp→0): 0.3156*P²/(9.871P+1)

So we need: [c0*P² + (c0*c2+c1)*P]/(P+c2) = 0.3156*P²/(9.871P+1)

This requires P+c2 = k*(9.871P+1), so c2 = 1/9.871, and the coefficient of P gives 1 = 9.871k, so k = 1/9.871.

Then numerator: c0*P² + (c0*c2+c1)*P should equal 0.3156/9.871 * P² = 0.03197*P²

So c0 = 0.03197 and c0*c2+c1 = 0, giving c1 = -c0*c2.

But we also need the P*exp(-0.054*t) term from GT. This candidate has no exp(t) term! It has c4*t (linear in t), c5*log(P*c6+1), c7/P. None of these can produce exp(-ct).

Setting c4=0 removes t dependence, but GT has exp(-ct) dependence on t.

Candidate 17 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 18: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(P*c2) + c3*exp(c4/(c5+t)) + c6*t² + c7*t + c8

P*c1*exp(P*c2): if c2=0, becomes P*c1. No way to get P²/(aP+1). exp(P*c2) is not rational. Also no P*exp(αt) term.

### Candidate 23: P*c0*exp(c1*t) + P*c2*t^c3 + P*c4/(P+c5) + c6*t + c7*t/(c8+t)

This is interesting! Let me analyze:
- P*c0*exp(c1*t): matches GT's first term ✓
- P*c4/(P+c5): rational in P. Let's check if this can match P²/(aP+1).

P*c4/(P+c5) = c4*P/(P+c5)

GT's second term: 0.3156*P²/(9.871P+1)

Can c4*P/(P+c5) = 0.3156*P²/(9.871P+1)? 

Left side is O(P) for large P (approaches c4), right side is O(P) for large P (approaches 0.3156P/9.871). Wait, right side grows linearly in P for large P, left side approaches constant c4. These are different asymptotic behaviors. So NO, P/(P+c5) ≠ P²/(aP+1) for any constants.

But wait, we have other terms: P*c2*t^c3. If c3=0, this becomes P*c2, adding to the P terms. And c6*t + c7*t/(c8+t) are t-only.

So the P-dependent part is: P*c0*exp(c1*t) + P*c2 + c4*P/(P+c5)

We need: P*c0*exp(c1*t) + c4*P/(P+c5) + P*c2 = 0.3156*P*exp(-0.054t) + 0.3156*P²/(9.871P+1)

The exp term matches. For the rest:
c4*P/(P+c5) + c2*P = 0.3156*P²/(9.871P+1)

[c4*P(9.871P+1) + c2*P(P+c5)(9.871P+1)] / [(P+c5)(9.871P+1)]

This is getting complicated. Let me try differently.

c2*P + c4*P/(P+c5) = [c2*P*(P+c5) + c4*P]/(P+c5) = P*[c2*P + c2*c5 + c4]/(P+c5)

= P*[c2*P + (c2*c5+c4)]/(P+c5)

GT: 0.3156*P²/(9.871P+1)

So we need: P*[c2*P + (c2*c5+c4)]/(P+c5) = 0.3156*P²/(9.871P+1)

This means: [c2*P + (c2*c5+c4)]/(P+c5) = 0.3156*P/(9.871P+1)

For these rational functions to be equal:
- Denominators must be proportional: P+c5 = k*(9.871P+1), so k=1/9.871, c5=1/9.871
- Numerators: c2*P + (c2*c5+c4) = (0.3156/9.871)*P = 0.03197*P

So c2 = 0.03197 and c2*c5+c4 = 0, giving c4 = -c2*c5 = -0.03197/9.871 ≈ -0.003238

This works for the P-dependent part! ✓

Now the t-dependent part: c6*t + c7*t/(c8+t). For GT, there should be NO extra t-dependence beyond the exp term. So we need c6=0 and c7=0.

With c6=0, c7=0, and c3=0 (so P*c2*t^c3 = P*c2):

GT = P*c0*exp(c1*t) + P*c2 + P*c4/(P+c5)

Yes! This matches! ✓

Candidate 23 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 24: P*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2/(P+c3) + c4*exp(c5/(c6+t)) + c7*exp(c8*t)*log(P*c9+1)
